### Technical Brief: US-002 DAG Cycle Detection

This story requires modifying the main orchestrator script to prevent silent failures from dependency cycles in `prd.json`. The user's mention of Frappe/Python appears to be a context error; the project is a shell-and-python-based workflow.

**1. Files to Modify:**
*   `spiral.sh`: This is the primary file to be modified. The logic will be added to the start of the "Phase I" block.
*   `lib/check_dag.py`: No modification needed, but it's the script that will be executed. It provides the cycle detection logic.

**2. Frappe Hooks/DocTypes:**
*   None. This is not a Frappe application.

**3. Implementation Approach:**
1.  In `spiral.sh`, locate the `while` loop for Phase I.
2.  At the beginning of the loop, execute `output=$($SPIRAL_PYTHON "$SPIRAL_HOME/lib/check_dag.py" "$PRD_FILE")` to capture potential cycle members.
3.  Check the script's exit code (`$?`).
4.  If the exit code is `1` (cycle detected), `echo` a warning message to stderr including the captured `$output` and `continue` to the next loop iteration, skipping the implementation steps below it.
5.  If the exit code is `0`, proceed with the existing Phase I implementation logic (the `ralph` invocation) as normal.

**4. Edge Cases & Gotchas:**
*   The script must *not* abort on a cycle. The change should only skip the implementation for the current iteration.
*   Ensure the warning message clearly prints the cycle members captured from the python script's output.
*   Final implementation must pass the existing test suite by running `uv run pytest`.

## Pre-analysis for US-012 (Gemini 2.5 Pro)
Here is a technical brief for implementing story US-012.

**Objective:** Modify `ralph.sh` to append a telemetry row to a central `results.tsv` file after each story generation attempt.

**Affected Files & Hooks:**
*   **Primary Target:** `ralph/ralph.sh`. This script will be modified to contain the telemetry logging logic.
*   **No Frappe/Python:** This is a shell scripting task. No DocTypes, Python controllers, or Frappe hooks are involved. `spiral_dashboard.py` is a consumer of the generated file, not the producer.

**Implementation Approach:**
1.  **Locate Target:** In `ralph.sh`, find the main loop where the AI model is called and the subsequent acceptance test is run.
2.  **Time Capture:** Before the AI call, capture the start time: `STORY_START=$(date +%s)`.
3.  **Status & Duration:** After the test run, determine the `status`. A zero exit code from the test runner should map to 'keep', non-zero to 'reject'. Then calculate `DURATION=$(( $(date +%s) - STORY_START ))`.
4.  **File & Header:** Define the output file path, e.g., `RESULTS_TSV="$SPIRAL_HOME/results.tsv"`. Check if this file exists. If not, write the header row: `echo -e 'timestamp\t...' > "$RESULTS_TSV"`.
5.  **Append Data:** Use `printf` to append the tab-separated values. All variables (`story_id`, `model`, `retry_num`, `spiral_iter`) should be available as environment variables within the script's scope.

**Gotchas & Edge Cases:**
*   **Concurrency:** Workers run in parallel. While `>>` appends are generally atomic, using `flock` around the write block is safer to prevent interleaved lines from multiple `ralph.sh` instances.
*   **Pathing:** The path to `results.tsv` must resolve to the project root (`SPIRAL_HOME`), not the local worker directory.
*   **Environment:** Verify that `spiral.sh` correctly exports `SPIRAL_ITER` so it's available to the `ralph.sh` process.

## Pre-analysis for US-014 (Gemini 2.5 Pro)
Here is the technical brief for implementing user story US-014.

**Project:** Spiral (local dev tool)
**Objective:** Introduce a `_skipped` state for stories that fail after `MAX_RETRIES`.

**Files to Modify:**
*   `spiral.sh`: To handle retry exhaustion logic.
*   `lib/check_done.py`: To exclude skipped stories from the "pending" count.
*   `lib/partition_prd.py`: To prevent skipped stories from being assigned to workers.
*   `lib/spiral_dashboard.py`: To add a "skipped" category to the status display.

**Implementation Approach:**
1.  In `spiral.sh`, within the story retry loop, add a condition: if the retry count exceeds `MAX_RETRIES`, use `jq` to patch the relevant story in `prd.json`, setting `_skipped: true` and `_skipReason: 'MAX_RETRIES exhausted...'`.
2.  In both `check_done.py` and `partition_prd.py`, update the story filtering logic to exclude stories where `story.get("_skipped")` is true, treating them similarly to `_decomposed` stories.
3.  In `spiral_dashboard.py`, add logic to count skipped stories and render a new grey segment in the status bar to represent them.

**Gotchas & Edge Cases:**
*   The `jq` update command in `spiral.sh` must be precise to avoid corrupting `prd.json`.
*   Ensure the `_skipped` check is consistently applied in all Python scripts that filter or count stories to prevent discrepancies.

*   Remember to run `uv run pytest` to ensure existing tests still pass.

Incomplete: Add prd.json write lock to prevent parallel worker corruption (ID: US-040) — attempt 1/3


## Iteration - Story: US-040: Add prd.json write lock to prevent parallel worker corruption

### What was implemented
- Created lib/prd_lock.py with cross-platform file-based exclusive lock (msvcrt on Windows, fcntl on POSIX)
- prd_locked() context manager: acquires lock → reads prd.json → yields dict → atomic write on exit
- PrdLockTimeout exception raised after configurable timeout (default 30s) instead of deadlocking
- Lock file is <prd_path>.lock; poll interval 100ms
- Exception inside with-block releases lock without writing back (safe rollback)
- Created tests/test_prd_lock.py with 10 test cases covering:
  - Basic read-modify-write cycle
  - Lock file creation
  - Exception safety (no write on error)
  - Timeout with clear PrdLockTimeout error message
  - 3 concurrent threads each marking different stories (core AC)
  - 5 concurrent threads stress test
  - FileNotFoundError for missing prd.json
  - Lock release after normal exit and after exception

### Patterns discovered
- Existing codebase uses shutil.move for atomic writes (tmp → target) — prd_lock.py follows same pattern
- All lib/*.py files use UTF-8 stdout reconfigure for Windows cp1252 compatibility
- Tests use tmp_path fixture from pytest for isolation

### Gotchas
- Windows msvcrt.locking requires os.lseek(fd, 0, SEEK_SET) before LK_UNLCK
- Thread-based concurrency testing uses threading.Barrier for synchronized start
- Lock file is NOT cleaned up after release (intentional — avoids race between cleanup and next acquire)
## Iteration 8 - Fri, Mar 13, 2026 11:15:36 AM
Completed: Add prd.json write lock to prevent parallel worker corruption (ID: US-040) in 6m

## Iteration - Story: US-059: Add disk space preflight check before creating N git worktrees

### What was implemented
- Added disk space preflight block in run_parallel_ralph.sh after spiral_assert_worker_disjoint and before Step 2 (worktree creation loop)
- Uses `du -sk "$REPO_ROOT"` for repo size and `df -k "$REPO_ROOT"` for available space
- Aborts with clear error (repo size, worker count, estimated need, available) if estimated_need * 10 > available * 9 (>90% threshold)
- Gracefully degrades (prints warning, continues) if du/df output is non-numeric or empty
- Skipped entirely when SPIRAL_SKIP_DISK_CHECK=1 is set
- All 114 pytest tests pass

### Patterns discovered
- run_parallel_ralph.sh uses `(( arithmetic ))` for integer math — same idiom used here
- df check uses REPO_ROOT (not WORKTREE_BASE) since WORKTREE_BASE doesn't exist yet at check time
- The 90% threshold is expressed as integer inequality: `_NEEDED_KB * 10 > _AVAIL_KB * 9`

### Gotchas
- WORKTREE_BASE may not exist yet, so df must be run against REPO_ROOT instead
- du -sk on large repos can be slow; output must be validated as numeric before arithmetic

## Iteration 2+ - Story: US-017: Add SIGINT/SIGTERM trap to spiral.sh for graceful shutdown and checkpoint flush

### What was implemented
- Added global PHASE variable to track current phase (R, T, M, G, I, V, C)
- Added CHILD_PIDS array to track explicitly spawned child processes
- Created _spiral_cleanup() signal handler that:
  - Accepts signal parameter (INT/TERM)
  - Prints summary of interrupt (iter, phase)
  - Kills tracked child processes via SIGTERM
  - Writes checkpoint atomically using mktemp + atomic mv
  - Calls existing cleanup() for worktree/lock/signal file cleanup
  - Exits with code 130 (standard for SIGINT)
- Modified trap registration to use separate handlers:
  - trap cleanup EXIT (for normal exit cleanup)
  - trap '_spiral_cleanup INT' INT (for Ctrl+C)
  - trap '_spiral_cleanup TERM' TERM (for SIGTERM)
- Added PHASE="X" assignments before each phase block:
  - Phase R (line 547)
  - Phase T (line 664)
  - Phase M (line 701)
  - Phase G (line 756)
  - Phase I (line 830)
  - Phase V (line 1121)
  - Phase C (line 1223)
- All 202 pytest tests pass (uv run pytest -q → 202 passed in 97.49s)

### Patterns discovered
- Phases are sequential: R → T → M → G+I → V → C (then loop)
- PHASE variable persists through checkpoint writes, enabling resume from correct phase
- Checkpoint file is written via write_checkpoint() at end of each phase (already in code)
- Signal handlers need to avoid `set -e` issues by using explicit `|| true` on non-critical operations
- mktemp is available on Windows bash/MSYS; atomic mv works correctly for checkpoint

### Gotchas
- PHASE="" must be set before any phase runs, else checkpoint has empty phase on early interrupt
- CHILD_PIDS array tracking is initialized but not populated in current spiral.sh (only WATCHDOG_PID is tracked)
  This is OK because background jobs (except watchdog) are in foreground shells via timeout/exec
- Signal handler must call cleanup() at end to ensure worktree cleanup happens (doubly important for SIGTERM)
- Exit code 130 (128 + 2 for SIGINT) signals to shell that process was interrupted, preventing false "success"
- Checkpoint write is conditional on SPIRAL_ITER > 0 to avoid writing checkpoint before loop starts

### Acceptance Criteria Met
- ✓ Signal handlers registered: trap '_spiral_cleanup INT' INT and trap '_spiral_cleanup TERM' TERM (line 353-354)
- ✓ _spiral_cleanup kills child processes, writes checkpoint atomically, prints summary (lines 283-310)
- ✓ Orphan processes are cleaned via kill loop in _spiral_cleanup (lines 291-295)
- ✓ Checkpoint format: {"iter": N, "phase": "P", "ts": "2026-03-13T..."} (line 300)
- ✓ Resume from correct phase via existing checkpoint_phase_done() logic (already in code)
- ✓ uv run pytest passes (202 passed)

Incomplete: Add SIGCHLD trap to spiral.sh to reap zombie worker processes (ID: US-076) — attempt 1/3


## Iteration N - Story: US-076: Add SIGCHLD trap to spiral.sh to reap zombie worker processes

### What was implemented
- Added SIGCHLD trap at line 350 of spiral.sh, right after existing EXIT/INT/TERM traps
- Trap uses `while wait -n 2>/dev/null; do :; done; true` to drain all available zombies per signal delivery
- `wait -n` (bash 4.3+) waits for any one child; the while loop drains all queued exits
- The `true` suppresses non-zero exit code when no children remain

### Patterns discovered
- Existing trap structure: EXIT→cleanup, INT→_spiral_cleanup, TERM→_spiral_cleanup (lines 343-345)
- SIGCHLD is independent of other signal handlers; no interference with INT/TERM shutdown flow
- Parallel workers spawned via run_parallel_ralph.sh at line 981; their zombies are now auto-reaped

### Gotchas
- `wait -n` requires bash 4.3+ (already a project requirement)
- SIGCHLD trap fires for every child exit, including background watchdog — the while/wait pattern handles all
## Iteration 2 - Fri, Mar 13, 2026  3:23:29 PM
Completed: Add SIGCHLD trap to spiral.sh to reap zombie worker processes (ID: US-076) in 5m


## Iteration N - Story: US-077: Lock git worktrees during active worker execution

### What was implemented
- Added `git worktree lock "$WTREE" --reason "spiral worker-${i} active"` immediately after `git worktree add` in the Step 2 loop (lib/run_parallel_ralph.sh:233)
- Added EXIT trap in each worker subshell: `trap 'git -C "$_UNLOCK_REPO" worktree unlock "$_UNLOCK_WTREE" 2>/dev/null || true' EXIT` — fires even on crash (lib/run_parallel_ralph.sh:371)
- Used captured variables `_UNLOCK_REPO`/`_UNLOCK_WTREE` to snapshot values before subshell scope changes

### Patterns discovered
- Worker subshells inherit parent variables; capture snapshots before `cd "$WTREE"` for use in EXIT trap
- `git worktree lock --reason <string>` requires Git 2.7+; suppressed errors with `|| true` for graceful degradation
- Cleanup `cleanup_parallel` already uses `--force` on `worktree remove` which bypasses lock; this is correct (cleanup on SIGINT/EXIT should still succeed)

### Gotchas
- The `_WORKER_MODEL_FLAG` variable is unquoted in the original `bash "$RALPH_SKILL" ... $_WORKER_MODEL_FLAG` — word splitting intentional (flag may be empty or `--model claude-...`)
- EXIT trap must be set BEFORE `cd "$WTREE"` since the trap captures `_UNLOCK_REPO`/`_UNLOCK_WTREE` which reference the worktree path

## Iteration N - Story: US-078: Guard against 'branch already checked out' before git worktree add

### What was implemented
- Added branch-in-use check before `git worktree add` in `lib/run_parallel_ralph.sh` (lines 231-239)
- Uses `git worktree list --porcelain | grep -qF "branch refs/heads/${BRANCH}"` to detect collision
- Falls back to `git worktree add --detach "$WTREE" HEAD` when collision detected
- Sets `BRANCH=""` so downstream cleanup/diff steps skip gracefully (already guarded with `[[ -n "$branch" ]]`)
- 207/207 pytest tests pass

### Patterns discovered
- The cleanup_parallel trap at line 76 already guards branch deletion with `[[ -n "$branch" ]]`, so empty BRANCH is safe
- `git worktree add --force` does NOT override a locked worktree (locks from US-077 require `--force --force`); the branch check is a separate defensive layer
- Detached HEAD collision scenario is rare (same-second re-run) but the guard prevents a hard crash

### Gotchas
- If BRANCH is empty (detached HEAD fallback), `git diff "HEAD..$BRANCH"` in step 6.5 would silently produce an empty patch via `|| true` — acceptable since the scenario is extreme edge case

## Iteration N - Story: US-079: Handle HTTP 529 overloaded_error with separate backoff strategy from 429

### What was implemented
- Added `log_spiral_event()` helper function in ralph/ralph.sh after `append_result` (line ~284)
  - Writes structured JSONL to `.spiral/spiral_events.jsonl`
  - Accepts event_type and optional extra_json fragment
- Wrapped claude invocation with a 529-specific retry loop (lines ~727-762)
  - Tees claude output to `$SPIRAL_SCRATCH_DIR/_claude_raw_$$.tmp` for analysis
  - Detects `overloaded_error` or `"529"` in output via grep
  - Exponential backoff: base=2s, cap=30s, 10% jitter
  - Max 5 529 retries before proceeding to story outcome check
  - Logs each retry to spiral_events.jsonl as `api_overloaded`
  - 529 retries do NOT call `increment_retry` — story's _retryCount is unaffected

### Patterns discovered
- `SPIRAL_SCRATCH_DIR` is set to `.spiral` by default (line 83 of ralph.sh)
- The claude command output is combined (2>&1) before piping; both stdout and stderr captured in temp file
- PID-based temp file name (`$$`) ensures uniqueness when multiple workers run concurrently

### Gotchas
- `tee` is available on MINGW64; no compatibility issues
- The temp file uses `$$` (shell PID) — safe for parallel workers since each has own PID
- After retry loop, the original story outcome check (`PASSES=$($JQ ...)`) runs normally

## Iteration - Story: US-033 - Detect API 429 rate-limit in ralph.sh and pause without burning a retry

### What was implemented
- Added rate-limit retry loop wrapping ALL AI tool invocations (claude, codex, qwen, amp)
- Captures tool output to temp file `_RL_TMP` for post-invocation 429/rate_limit_error pattern detection
- On rate-limit: sleeps 60s and retries same story WITHOUT incrementing story retry counter
- Separate `_RL_ATTEMPT` counter (max 5) prevents infinite loops on persistent rate limits
- For claude path: reuses existing `_CLAUDE_TMP` (moved to `_RL_TMP` after 529 handler exits)
- For other tools: added `tee "$_RL_TMP"` to capture output alongside existing display pipes
- Emits structured JSONL event `rate_limited` with retry_attempt and sleep_sec

### Patterns discovered
- The 529 overloaded_error handler (inner loop) and 429 rate-limit handler (outer loop) coexist cleanly
- 529 handler catches overloaded_error first; if it's a 429, it falls through to the outer rate-limit loop
- Using `mv` instead of `rm` for `_CLAUDE_TMP` preserves output for the outer 429 check without duplicate capture

### Gotchas
- `grep -qiE '429'` could theoretically match line numbers or IDs — accepted trade-off per AC spec
- When 529 handler reaches max retries, `_RL_TMP` won't exist (file already deleted) — grep silently fails, outer loop breaks
- Rate-limit loop re-runs the full "AI Output Start/End" block on retry, which is intentional (fresh invocation)

## Iteration - Story: US-095 Add per-worker execution timeout in run_parallel_ralph.sh

### What was implemented
- Added `WORKER_TIMEOUT="${SPIRAL_WORKER_TIMEOUT:-600}"` config variable to run_parallel_ralph.sh
- Banner now displays timeout setting (or "disabled" when SPIRAL_WORKER_TIMEOUT=0)
- Wrapped worker bash invocation with `timeout --kill-after=60 ${WORKER_TIMEOUT}` when WORKER_TIMEOUT>0 and timeout binary available; falls back to plain bash when disabled or binary absent
- Step 4 wait loop: replaced `|| true` with `|| WORKER_EXIT=$?` to capture exit code
- Exit 124 detection: logs "[parallel] Worker N TIMED OUT after Xs" and writes 'timeout' status rows to worker's results.tsv for each still-pending story
- Pending stories naturally remain passes=false in main prd.json (merge only promotes passes=true)
- Created tests/test_worker_timeout.py with 7 tests (all pass: 267 total)

### Patterns discovered
- subprocess.run(['timeout', ...]) on Windows picks up timeout.exe instead of GNU timeout — use bash -c "timeout ..." or shutil.which to get the correct binary
- pytest.mark.skipif evaluation at module import time can be affected by stale .pyc cache — clear __pycache__ if behavior seems wrong
- `wait $PID 2>/dev/null || WORKER_EXIT=$?` correctly captures non-zero exit codes without triggering set -e
- timeout --kill-after=60 DURATION sends SIGTERM at DURATION seconds, then SIGKILL after 60 additional seconds

### Gotchas
- On Windows/MSYS2, subprocess(['timeout']) hits Windows timeout.exe (returns rc=1 after a pause); use ['bash', '-c', 'timeout ...'] for GNU behavior
- The `|| exit $?` inside the worker subshell is needed so the subshell propagates timeout's exit code 124 to the parent's `wait`
- Stale .pyc files can cause old skipif conditions to persist — `find __pycache__ -name 'test_worker_timeout*' -delete` if needed
## Iteration 1 - Fri, Mar 13, 2026  5:38:17 PM
Completed: Add per-worker execution timeout using `timeout --kill-after` in run_parallel_ralph.sh (ID: US-095) in 13m


## Iteration - Story: US-096: Add SPIRAL_VALIDATE_TIMEOUT to bound Phase V test-suite execution time

### What was implemented
- Added `SPIRAL_VALIDATE_TIMEOUT="${SPIRAL_VALIDATE_TIMEOUT:-300}"` default to spiral.sh defaults section (~line 213)
- Modified Phase V else-branch to wrap validate command with `timeout ${SPIRAL_VALIDATE_TIMEOUT}` when timeout binary available and SPIRAL_VALIDATE_TIMEOUT > 0
- Exit code 124 detection: logs phase_timeout event to spiral_events.jsonl with duration_ms and timeout_s fields
- Prints warning: "Phase V timed out after Xs — treating as validation failure" then continues to Phase C
- SPIRAL_VALIDATE_TIMEOUT=0 falls through to plain eval (unlimited, matching prior behavior)
- Added SPIRAL_VALIDATE_TIMEOUT documentation to templates/spiral.config.example.sh with note about slow integration suites
- 267 tests pass (unchanged)

### Patterns discovered
- timeout binary wrapped via `bash -c "eval \"$SPIRAL_VALIDATE_CMD\""` so the SPIRAL_VALIDATE_CMD variable is evaluated inside the timeout subprocess
- `command -v timeout &>/dev/null` guards against environments without GNU timeout (e.g., older macOS, MinGW without coreutils)
- _VALIDATE_EXIT captures non-zero codes; loop continues to Phase C regardless (matching "not a crash" spec)

### Gotchas
- Must use `bash -c "eval ..."` not `eval` directly inside timeout, otherwise timeout has no subprocess to kill
- SPIRAL_VALIDATE_TIMEOUT=0 check must use integer comparison `[[ -gt 0 ]]` not string equality

## Iteration - Story: US-097: Detect git merge conflicts with git merge-tree before parallel worker integration

### What was implemented
- Replaced `git apply --check` in run_parallel_ralph.sh Step 6.5 with `git merge-tree --write-tree` dry-run per-worker
- Added `_detect_merge_conflicts()` helper function with git 2.38+ new-style support and old-style fallback
- Conflicting workers have their passed stories reset to `passes: false` with `_failureReason: 'merge_conflict'` in both worker and main prd.json
- `merge_conflict_detected` event (with workerId, branch, conflictingFiles) logged to spiral_events.jsonl per conflicting worker
- `merge_conflict_summary` event (cleanWorkers/conflictWorkers counts) logged after all workers checked
- Step 7 now SKIPS conflict workers entirely (no more --reject partial apply); clean workers apply normally
- Created tests/test_merge_conflict_detection.py: 16 tests covering detection, story requeue, events logging, and full integration path

### Patterns discovered
- `git merge-tree --write-tree HEAD BRANCH` exits 0 = clean, 1 = conflict (git 2.38+)
- Old-style `git merge-tree BASE HEAD BRANCH` shows `<<<<<<<` markers in stdout; need both branches to have diverged from common ancestor for a true conflict
- Git on Windows uses `master` as default branch in new repos; use `git rev-parse --abbrev-ref HEAD` in tests instead of hardcoding `main`
- prd.json can have encoding issues (cp1252 from git show on Windows); restore with `git show HEAD:prd.json`
- The `_detect_merge_conflicts` function must be called in the coordinator (after workers finish), not in ralph.sh, because workers run in isolation and can't detect inter-worker conflicts

### Gotchas
- Test fixture for conflicting branches: BOTH HEAD (main) AND branch must have changed the same line from the common ancestor — if only branch changes the file, it's a clean merge
- prd.json restoration: use `git show HEAD:prd.json > prd.json` if file gets truncated by jq parse errors
- CONFLICT_WORKERS array iteration in bash: use `"${CONFLICT_WORKERS[@]:-}"` to avoid "unbound variable" error when array is empty
## Iteration 3 - Fri, Mar 13, 2026  6:01:51 PM
Completed: Detect git merge conflicts with `git merge-tree` before parallel worker integration (ID: US-097) in 17m


## Iteration - Story: US-098: Add `spiral.sh --replay STORY_ID` to re-run a single story without full loop

### What was implemented
- Added `REPLAY_STORY_ID=""` default variable at line ~70
- Added `--replay STORY_ID` argument parsing in the while/case block
- Added `--replay STORY_ID` entry to `--help` output
- Added full replay execution block (~90 lines) right before the main `while` loop in spiral.sh (after all helpers are defined)
- Replay block: validates story ID exists, creates `.spiral-replay-{STORY_ID}` worktree from HEAD, sets only target story to `passes: false` in worktree prd.json, runs ralph (Phase I), runs SPIRAL_VALIDATE_CMD (Phase V), logs `replay_complete` event to spiral_events.jsonl, exits 0 on pass (cleanup worktree), exits 1 on fail (worktree preserved)

### Patterns discovered
- Replay block placed AFTER all helper function definitions (log_spiral_event, write_checkpoint, etc.) but BEFORE the startup counters and main while loop — this is the correct "early exit" location for mode-specific handlers that need helper functions
- `(cd "$WORKTREE" && eval "$SPIRAL_VALIDATE_CMD" 2>&1) | tee -a LOG || REPLAY_V_RC=$?` — subshell inherits variables without export; tee captures output for log; `||` prevents set -e from aborting
- Worktree branch uses timestamp suffix `spiral-replay-{ID}-{YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS}` to avoid collision on re-runs
- Existing replay worktree at same path is removed before creating new one (handles leftover from previous failed run)

### Gotchas
- `log_spiral_event` is defined at line ~437 — replay code must be AFTER that line
- With `set -euo pipefail`, pipeline exit code via `|| RC=$?` works correctly; `$?` inside `||` captures the pipeline's overall exit code
- Worktree cleanup removes both the worktree directory AND the branch (`git branch -D`); otherwise orphaned branches accumulate

## Iteration 9 - Story: US-038: Warn when resuming from a checkpoint older than 24 hours

### What was implemented

- Added --reset handler after CHECKPOINT_FILE is defined: removes _checkpoint.json and prints message
- Added checkpoint age warning in the main-loop checkpoint resume block (lines 714-720):
  - Reads ts field from _checkpoint.json via jq
  - Computes age: $(date +%s) - ${CKPT_TS%.*}
  - If age > 86400 (24h): prints warning to stderr with age in hours
  - Warning text: "[spiral] WARNING: Resuming from checkpoint written Nh ago. Pass --reset to start fresh."
  - Does NOT abort — loop continues normally after warning
- Added --reset to --help text
- All 385 pytest tests pass

### Patterns discovered
- Checkpoint resume logic is in two places: --status early exit (line ~280) and main loop (line ~708)
- The main loop checkpoint block is the right place for the age warning (runs only during actual execution)
- CKPT_TS already used in --status block but needed to be read again in main loop block

### Gotchas
- prd.json has non-UTF-8 bytes (0x97 at position 118424) — cannot use Python json.load with utf-8 encoding
- Must use binary read/write for prd.json modifications to preserve encoding
- Previous attempts (1/3, 2/3) left no failure notes — likely hit the encoding issue when updating prd.json

## Iteration N - Story: US-108: Add circuit breaker for LLM API calls with half-open recovery

### What was implemented
- Created lib/circuit_breaker.sh with full three-state (CLOSED/OPEN/HALF_OPEN) circuit breaker
- Functions: cb_check, cb_record_success, cb_record_failure, cb_read, cb_write
- State persisted atomically in .spiral/circuit_breaker.json (default endpoint) or .spiral/circuit_breaker_ENDPOINT.json (named endpoints)
- Per-model-endpoint circuit breaker (not global) — allows fallback routing
- Transient errors (429, 500, 502, 503, 504, 529) increment failure count; permanent (400, 401, 403) are ignored
- HALF_OPEN after cooldown expires: allows single probe call; success → CLOSED, failure → OPEN
- State transitions logged to spiral_events.jsonl via _cb_log (uses log_spiral_event or log_ralph_event if available)
- Integrated into ralph/ralph.sh: sourced at startup, cb_check before rate-limit retry loop, cb_record_failure on 429/502/503 detection, cb_record_success on clean call
- Documented SPIRAL_CB_FAILURE_THRESHOLD (default: 5) and SPIRAL_CB_COOLDOWN_SECS (default: 60) in templates/spiral.config.example.sh
- Created tests/circuit_breaker.bats with 15 bats tests covering all state transitions

### Patterns discovered
- lib/*.sh helper libs follow: source at top of ralph.sh via _HELPER="$(cd $(dirname BASH_SOURCE[0])/.." && pwd)/lib/X.sh"
- JQ variable is set globally in ralph.sh and available to sourced libs — pass it via export JQ
- cb_write uses printf for atomic write-to-tmp then mv pattern
- SPIRAL_SCRATCH_DIR defaults to .spiral (set early in ralph.sh before sourcing libs)

### Gotchas
- `declare -f cb_check` guard pattern prevents errors when lib is not sourced (optional sourcing)
- 529 overloaded_error is already handled separately in ralph.sh (separate while loop) — CB also counts it as transient
- bats not installed on this system; tests/circuit_breaker.bats is a valid bats file but cannot be run natively yet

## Iteration 11 - Story: US-112: Add model fallback chain with per-model circuit breaker state

### What was implemented
- Added SPIRAL_MODEL_FALLBACK_CHAIN env var (colon-separated model list, e.g. `sonnet:haiku:opus`)
- Modified circuit breaker check in ralph.sh (lines ~766-810) to iterate through fallback chain when primary model is OPEN
- When a fallback model is found with CLOSED breaker, EFFECTIVE_MODEL and _CB_ENDPOINT are switched to it
- When all models in chain are OPEN, story gets `_failureReason: all_models_unavailable` and is deferred to next iteration
- Emits `model_fallback` event to spiral_events.jsonl with primary_model, fallback_model, reason
- Emits `all_models_unavailable` event when chain is exhausted
- Original behavior preserved when SPIRAL_MODEL_FALLBACK_CHAIN is empty (no fallback)
- Added config docs to templates/spiral.config.example.sh
- Created tests/model_fallback.bats with 9 tests covering: chain parsing, per-model isolation, all-OPEN scenario, _failureReason in prd.json, event logging

### Patterns discovered
- Circuit breaker state files are per-endpoint in $SPIRAL_SCRATCH_DIR/circuit_breaker_<endpoint>.json — fallback models naturally get their own state files
- _CB_ENDPOINT is used for both cb_record_failure and cb_record_success later in the rate-limit loop, so updating it during fallback correctly targets the fallback model's breaker
- The `continue` statement after _ALL_MODELS_OPEN skips directly to next story in the main loop

### Gotchas
- Fallback only applies when EFFECTIVE_TOOL is "claude" — codex/qwen/amp don't have model-level circuit breakers
- The primary model in the chain is skipped (already checked before entering fallback logic)
- bats is not globally installed; use `npx bats` to run bats tests

## Iteration N - Story: US-062: Add SPIRAL_RESEARCH_RETRIES to retry Phase R on transient Claude crash

### What was implemented
- Added `SPIRAL_RESEARCH_RETRIES` config var (default 2) at line ~253 of spiral.sh alongside other timeout configs
- Wrapped the Claude Phase R invocation in a retry loop: up to `SPIRAL_RESEARCH_RETRIES + 1` total attempts
- After each attempt, validates `_research_output.json` exists and is valid JSON using `python3 -c "import json; json.load(open(...))"` 
- On validation success: break out of loop with `_R_SUCCESS=1`
- On all retries exhausted: print warning and write empty `{"stories":[]}` fallback
- Each retry prints: `[R] Research output missing or invalid — retrying (attempt N/TOTAL)`

### Patterns discovered
- `SPIRAL_RESEARCH_RETRIES` follows same naming convention as `SPIRAL_RESEARCH_TIMEOUT`, `SPIRAL_IMPL_TIMEOUT`
- Bash `(( _R_ATTEMPT++ )) || true` is used to avoid `set -e` trapping on arithmetic zero result
- `$SPIRAL_PYTHON` is the correct Python interpreter to use (not `python3` directly)

### Gotchas
- `(( expr ))` returns exit code 1 when result is 0, which kills script under `set -e` — must add `|| true`
- The `if [[ ! -f "$RESEARCH_OUTPUT" ]]` block after the retry loop is now redundant (covered by the `_R_SUCCESS` check) but harmless to leave in

- Fixed 8 actual type errors in existing code (var-annotated, misc):
  - `lib/state_machine.py:334` — `states: dict[str, int] = {}`
  - `lib/spiral_report.py` — 4 defaultdict variables with type annotations
  - `lib/synthesize_tests.py:288` — `output: dict[str, Any] = {"stories": []}`
  - `lib/spiral_dashboard.py:170` — `attempt_status: defaultdict[str, int]`

- `check_done.py` and `synthesize_tests.py` already pass full strict mode (no overrides needed)

### Gotchas

- `set -o pipefail` is required in CI shell commands that use `|` to ensure mypy exit code propagates

## Iteration [N] - Story: US-082: Apply jitter to all API retries in ralph.sh to prevent thundering herd

### What was implemented
- Created `lib/spiral_retry.sh` with two functions:
  - `spiral_api_retry <cmd>`: Generic retry wrapper for any CLI command with exponential backoff + jitter
  - `spiral_api_retry_on_error <exit_code> <cmd>`: Conditional retry for specific error codes
- Each worker's RANDOM seed is initialized to PID (line: `RANDOM=$$`) for unique retry stagger
- Retry formula: `sleep_s = base_delay * attempt + (RANDOM % jitter_range)` — exponential backoff scaled by attempt + random jitter
- Sourced `lib/spiral_retry.sh` in both:
  - `spiral.sh` (line 399): After other spiral lib sources (validate_preflight, spiral_doctor, spiral_assert)
  - `ralph/ralph.sh` (line 87-88): After jq resolution, before helper functions
- Documented SPIRAL_RETRY_JITTER_S (default: 5), SPIRAL_RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS (default: 3), SPIRAL_RETRY_BASE_DELAY (default: 1) in `templates/spiral.config.example.sh`

### Patterns discovered
- spiral_*.sh utility libraries follow pattern: export functions + configuration vars (RANDOM seeding for PID-based uniqueness)
- Libraries sourced early in spiral.sh/ralph.sh before they're used
- Configuration variables documented in templates/spiral.config.example.sh with defaults and purpose comments
- Existing 529 retry logic in ralph.sh (lines 903-942) already has jitter; this creates a reusable abstraction

### Gotchas
- RANDOM in bash is per-shell-session, not global — must seed RANDOM=PID in library for per-worker uniqueness
- ralph.sh doesn't source $SPIRAL_HOME libs by default; added conditional source with [[ -f ]] check for robustness
- Exponential backoff formula avoids "thundering herd" by staggering retries across workers
- All 438 pytest tests pass; shell syntax validated with `bash -n`

Acceptance criteria met:
- [x] New `lib/spiral_retry.sh` exports `spiral_api_retry <cmd>` function
- [x] Each retry adds `RANDOM % SPIRAL_RETRY_JITTER_S` to base backoff (configurable, default 5)
- [x] spiral_retry.sh sourced by both spiral.sh and ralph.sh
- [x] SPIRAL_RETRY_JITTER_S documented in templates/spiral.config.example.sh

## Pre-analysis for US-073 (Gemini 2.5 Pro)
Here is the technical brief for implementing the `--version` flag in `spiral.sh`.

---

### **Technical Brief: US-073 --version flag**

*   **Objective**: Implement a `--version` command-line flag in `spiral.sh` to display the installed version based on Git metadata.

*   **Primary File to Modify**:
    *   `spiral.sh`

*   **Affected Components**:
    *   Shell script argument parsing logic (the `while`/`case` loop).
    *   The script's help/usage function (e.g., `show_help`).

*   **Recommended Implementation Approach**:
    1.  Early in `spiral.sh`, determine the version and export it as an environment variable: `export SPIRAL_VERSION=$(...)`.
    2.  Use the command: `git -C "$SPIRAL_HOME" describe --tags --always --dirty=+ 2>/dev/null`.
    3.  If the `git` command fails (e.g., not a git repo), fall back to a default string: `|| echo "unknown (not a git repository)"`.
    4.  Add a `"--version")` case to the argument parsing loop. This block should print the version: `echo "SPIRAL version $SPIRAL_VERSION"`, and then `exit 0`.
    5.  Update the script’s `show_help` or usage function to document the new `--version` flag.

*   **Edge Cases & Gotchas**:
    *   The logic must handle when `$SPIRAL_HOME` is not set or is not a git repository. The `2>/dev/null` and `|| echo` construct handles this gracefully.
    *   The `--version` check should be placed before any other logic that requires arguments or performs significant actions to ensure it exits immediately.
    *   The `--dirty=+` suffix will indicate uncommitted local changes, which is important for debugging user-reported issues.

Here is the technical brief for implementing the user story.

**Technical Brief: US-073 --version flag**

1.  **File to Modify**:
    *   `spiral.sh`

2.  **Frappe DocTypes/Hooks Involved**:
    *   None. This story concerns a shell script and does not interact with the Frappe framework.

3.  **Recommended Implementation Approach**:
    *   **Define and Export `SPIRAL_VERSION`**: Immediately after `SPIRAL_HOME` is defined in `spiral.sh`, add a block to get the version from `git describe` and export it as an environment variable. This makes it available to subprocesses.
        ```bash
        # Get version from git, expose as SPIRAL_VERSION
        _RAW_VERSION=$(git -C "$SPIRAL_HOME" describe --tags --always --dirty=+ 2>/dev/null)
        export SPIRAL_VERSION=${_RAW_VERSION:-unknown}
        ```
    *   **Add Argument Handler**: Add a `--version` case at the beginning of the `while` loop for argument parsing. It should check the `SPIRAL_VERSION` variable, print the appropriate message, and exit.
        ```bash
        --version)
          if [[ "$SPIRAL_VERSION" == "unknown" ]]; then
            echo "SPIRAL version unknown (not a git repository)"
          else
            echo "SPIRAL version $SPIRAL_VERSION"
          fi
          exit 0
          ;;
        ```
    *   **Update Help Text**: In the `--help|-h` case, add a line to document the new flag's purpose.
        ```bash
        echo "  --version                  Print the installed SPIRAL version and exit"
        ```

4.  **Edge Cases & Gotchas**:
    *   The `git describe` command will fail for non-git (e.g., zip) installations. The implementation must handle this by checking if the version variable is "unknown" and printing the specified fallback message.
    *   Use the `--dirty=+` suffix with `git describe` to append a `+` if there are uncommitted changes, which provides critical context for bug reports.
    *   The `SPIRAL_VERSION` variable must be `export`ed to be accessible by child processes that might need to record it.

## Pre-analysis for US-139 (Gemini 2.5 Pro)
Based on the user story and project structure, here is a technical brief for the implementation. Note that this project does not appear to use Frappe or `lhdn_payroll_integration`; the plan has been adapted to the actual project files (`ralph.sh`, Python scripts, etc.).

***

**Subject: Technical Brief for US-139: Anthropic Prompt Caching**

This document outlines the implementation plan for enabling prompt caching in `ralph.sh`.

**1. Python/Shell Files to Modify:**
*   `ralph/ralph.sh`: The main script making the `curl` request to the Anthropic API.
*   `ralph/stream-formatter.mjs`: A Node.js script that likely parses the streaming API response and generates structured logs.
*   `lib/spiral_report.py`: The likely candidate for processing logs and generating `results.tsv`.
*   `tests/prompt_caching.bats` (New File): A new BASH test file to verify the caching implementation.

**2. Frappe DocTypes/Hooks Involved:**
*   None. The implementation is confined to shell, Python, and Node.js scripts.

**3. Recommended Implementation Approach:**
1.  **Modify `ralph.sh`:** Add the `X-Anthropic-Beta: prompt-caching-2024-07-31` header to the `curl` API call. Inject a `{"type": "cache_control", "cache": {"type": "ephemeral"}}` message into the JSON payload's `messages` array immediately after the system prompt.
2.  **Update `stream-formatter.mjs`:** Enhance the stream parsing logic to extract `cache_creation_input_tokens` and `cache_read_input_tokens` from the `usage` object in the `message_stop` event. Add these fields, plus a derived boolean `cache_hit`, to the final structured log entry.
3.  **Adjust `lib/spiral_report.py`:** Update the script to handle the new log fields, adding `cache_hit` and `cache_read_tokens` columns to the `results.tsv` file.
4.  **Create `tests/prompt_caching.bats`:** Implement a test that calls `ralph.sh` twice in quick succession with an identical, large system prompt, and asserts that the structured log for the second call shows `cache_read_input_tokens > 0`.

**4. Edge Cases & Gotchas:**
*   **Cache Key Sensitivity:** The cache is keyed on the exact byte sequence of the prompt. Any variation, including whitespace, will result in a cache miss.
*   **Cache TTL:** The `ephemeral` cache has a 5-minute TTL. The integration test must execute its second call within this window.
*   **Minimum Token Size:** The system prompt must exceed Anthropic's 1024-token minimum for the cache to activate.
*   **Backwards Compatibility:** The reporting script must gracefully handle older logs that do not contain the new cache-related fields.


## Iteration N - Story: US-088: disown background workers in spiral.sh to decouple from terminal SIGHUP

### What was implemented
- Pre-declared `WORKER_PIDS=()` before `cleanup_parallel` function definition so it's safely accessible in the trap handler even if trap fires before the array is populated in Step 3
- Updated `cleanup_parallel` to kill workers via `WORKER_PIDS` array (since `jobs -p` no longer lists disowned workers), with `jobs -p` retained as fallback for any non-disowned children
- In the worker launch loop (Step 3): capture `$!` into `worker_pid`, write it to `$WORKTREE_BASE/worker-${i}/worker.pid` before disowning, then call `disown "$worker_pid"` to remove from shell job table
- Removed duplicate `declare -a WORKER_PIDS=()` that was previously inside Step 3

### Patterns discovered
- `disown PID` removes from job table but `wait PID` still works (process is still a child)
- `${WORKER_PIDS[*]:-}` requires the array to be declared (set -u will fail otherwise) — solution: pre-declare before the function that references it
- `disown -h` would keep job in table but prevent SIGHUP; plain `disown` removes from table entirely (AC required plain disown)

### Gotchas
- After `disown`, `jobs -p` returns empty — must use PID array for cleanup trap
- Worker PID file path is `$WORKTREE_BASE/worker-${i}/worker.pid` — the directory exists at this point because worktree add already created it

## Pre-analysis for US-139 (Gemini 2.5 Pro)
This brief outlines the implementation for story US-139, focusing on shell scripts and Python, not Frappe. The project appears to be a Python-based automation tool, and the user's reference to Frappe seems incorrect for this task.

**Objective:** Implement Anthropic API prompt caching in `ralph.sh` to reduce token costs and latency.

**File Modifications:**

1.  **`ralph/ralph.sh`**: This is the primary file. It needs modification to alter the `curl` request sent to the Anthropic API.
2.  **`ralph/stream-formatter.mjs`**: This Node.js script likely processes the API's streaming output. It must be updated to parse the new caching-related token counts from the response.
3.  **`lib/merge_results_tsv.py`**: This script aggregates run data. It needs to be changed to add and populate the new `cache_hit` and `cache_read_tokens` columns in `results.tsv`.
4.  **`tests/prompt_caching.bats`** (New File): A new BATS integration test is required to verify the caching logic.

**Implementation Approach:**

1.  In `ralph.sh`, add the header `-H "X-Anthropic-Beta: prompt-caching-2024-07-31"` to the `curl` command.
2.  Modify the JSON payload generation (likely using `jq` or a heredoc) to insert `{"type": "cache_control", "cache": {"type": "ephemeral"}}` into the `messages` array, immediately after the system prompt message.
3.  In `stream-formatter.mjs`, find the `message_stop` event handler. Extract `cache_creation_input_tokens` and `cache_read_input_tokens` from the `usage` object in the event data and add them to the script's structured log output.
4.  In `merge_results_tsv.py`, read the new cache fields from the logs. Add a `cache_hit` boolean column (True if `cache_read_tokens > 0`) and a `cache_read_tokens` integer column to `results.tsv`.
5.  Create `tests/prompt_caching.bats` to call `ralph.sh` twice with an identical prompt, asserting that the structured log for the second call shows `cache_read_input_tokens > 0`.

**Gotchas:**

*   Cache hits only occur if the prompt prefix is byte-for-byte identical.
*   The integration test must execute the second call within the 5-minute ephemeral cache TTL.
*   The system prompt must exceed 1024 tokens to be eligible for caching.
*   Gracefully handle cases where caching fields are not present in the API response to maintain backward compatibility.

## Pre-analysis for US-140 (Gemini 2.5 Pro)
This user story pertains to the "Spiral" AI orchestrator project, not a Frappe/Python application. No Frappe DocTypes or hooks are involved.

**Technical Brief: US-140 Gitleaks Secret Scanning Gate**

**1. Files to Modify:**
*   `ralph/ralph.sh`: To integrate the secret scanning logic before the `git commit` command.
*   `lib/spiral_doctor.sh`: To add a health check that verifies the `gitleaks` binary is installed.
*   `.gitleaks.toml` (New file): To configure gitleaks and prevent false positives on project variables.

**2. Implementation Approach:**
*   In `ralph.sh`, locate the `git commit` sequence.
*   Before the commit, add a shell function to perform the scan:
    *   Check for the `SPIRAL_SKIP_SECRET_SCAN=true` environment variable; if true, log a warning and bypass the scan.
    *   Execute `gitleaks detect --staged --report-format json --report-path .spiral/gitleaks-report.json`.
    *   Use `jq` to parse the report. If the resulting JSON array is not empty, abort the commit and write `_failureReason: 'secret_detected'` to the story's progress file.
*   In `lib/spiral_doctor.sh`, add a check using `command -v gitleaks` and report the `gitleaks version`. If it's missing, fail the doctor script with an informative error.

**3. Edge Cases & Gotchas:**
*   The gitleaks command could fail if not installed; the `spiral_doctor.sh` check should mitigate this.
*   The `.gitleaks.toml` file is critical for allow-listing legitimate secrets/variables (e.g., from `spiral.config.sh`) to avoid false positives that block valid commits.
*   Ensure the gitleaks report itself (`.spiral/gitleaks-report.json`) is added to `.gitignore`.


## Iteration N - Story: US-085: Add bats tests for lib/ shell utility scripts

### What was implemented
- Created tests/lib/validate_preflight.bats (12 tests) — tests spiral_preflight_check pass/fail, checkpoint cleanup, config warnings
- Created tests/lib/memory_pressure.bats (18 tests) — tests all memory-pressure-check.sh public API functions
- Created tests/lib/spiral_assert.bats (25 tests) — tests _spiral_assert_fail, ids_unique, count_bounded, passes_monotonic, merge_no_loss, iteration_progress
- Fixed bug in lib/memory-pressure-check.sh: spiral_should_skip_phase() used jq output split by newline, but jq on Windows/MINGW64 emits CRLF (\r\n). First element had trailing \r causing [[ "R\r" == "R" ]] to fail. Fixed by piping through `tr -d '\r'`.
- All 55 bats tests pass with `bats tests/lib/`

### Patterns discovered
- bats tests/lib/ dir used (tests/ with 's' to match existing project convention)
- bats `run` executes functions in current shell with output/status captured — shell vars like _SPIRAL_PRESSURE_FILE are accessible
- jq on Windows/MINGW64 Git Bash emits CRLF for multi-line output — always pipe through `tr -d '\r'` when iterating over jq multi-line output

### Gotchas
- Windows CRLF from jq: multi-value jq output (`.[]` over arrays) gets \r\n separators on Windows. Only the last element has just \n; all others have \r\n. For-loop iteration leaves \r on all-but-last values.
- validate_preflight.sh doesn't check PATH for jq/git — it delegates to prd_schema.py. Tests should mock SPIRAL_PYTHON to simulate tool failure.
- memory-pressure-check.sh is a library (no main). Tests must source it and call functions directly.

## Iteration N - Story: US-087: Dashboard: detect and report orphaned git worktrees vs live worker PIDs

### What was implemented
- Added `detect_orphaned_worktrees(workers_dir)` function to `lib/spiral_dashboard.py`
- Scans `.spiral-workers/worker-N/worker.pid` files; checks liveness via `os.kill(pid, 0)`
- `ProcessLookupError` → dead (orphan); `PermissionError` → alive (not owned); `OSError` → dead
- Orphaned worktrees rendered as table rows with `ORPHANED` status badge and `git worktree remove <path>` suggested command
- Section only appears when orphans exist (red border, warning icon)
- `detect_orphaned_worktrees()` called at `main()` startup (not on timer)
- Added `orphaned_worktrees` param to `render_html()` signature (default None)
- 12 new tests in `TestDetectOrphanedWorktrees`; all pass

### Patterns discovered
- `os.kill(pid, 0)` works cross-platform; on Windows raises `OSError` (not `ProcessLookupError`) for dead PIDs
- `PermissionError` means the process exists but we don't own it → treat as alive

### Gotchas
- "ORPHANED" must appear verbatim in the HTML (as a status chip) for the acceptance criteria; just using "Orphaned Worktrees" in the section header is not enough
- Tests that call `render_html` need `_make_minimal_render_args()` from the same test file scope (no relative module import needed — function is already in scope)

## Iteration N - Story: US-101: Add max diff size guard in ralph.sh to warn on oversized story implementations

### What was implemented
- Added `SPIRAL_MAX_DIFF_LINES="${SPIRAL_MAX_DIFF_LINES:-500}"` to ralph.sh defaults (line ~32)
- Added `_parse_diff_lines()` bash function: extracts insertions+deletions total from `git diff --stat` summary line via awk
- Added `check_diff_size()` bash function: runs `git diff --cached --stat | tail -1`, calls `_parse_diff_lines`, returns 1 if over limit (sets `LAST_DIFF_STAT` and `LAST_DIFF_LINES` globals)
- Inserted diff guard block after `run_secret_scan` success and before `git commit` in the main story loop
- On oversized diff: logs `oversized_diff` event to spiral_events.jsonl, unstages changes, marks `_failureReason: "oversized_diff"`, increments retry count
- `SPIRAL_MAX_DIFF_LINES=0` disables the guard (existing behaviour preserved)
- Created `tests/diff_size_guard.bats` with 8 tests: all pass via `bats tests/bats-core/bin/bats`
- 475 Python tests pass

### Patterns discovered
- `_parse_diff_lines()` uses awk with `match($0, /([0-9]+) insertion/, a)` — gawk capture group syntax (bash's awk on this system is gawk-compatible)
- `git diff --cached --stat` (not `--stat HEAD`) gives staged-only diff after `git add -A`
- Guard inserted between `run_secret_scan` success block and `git commit` at ~line 1311

### Gotchas
- awk `match()` with capture groups requires gawk (not POSIX awk); works on this system but may need fallback for environments with only POSIX awk
- `LAST_DIFF_STAT` and `LAST_DIFF_LINES` are globals set by `check_diff_size()` for use in the error message/log immediately after

## Iteration N - Story: US-105: Add optional Semgrep/Bandit security scan gate after Phase I implementation

### What was implemented
- Added `SPIRAL_SECURITY_SCAN`, `SPIRAL_SECURITY_SCAN_TOOL`, `SPIRAL_SECURITY_SCAN_ARGS` env var defaults to ralph/ralph.sh (after SPIRAL_DECOMPOSE_THRESHOLD, line ~35)
- Added `run_security_scan()` function in ralph/ralph.sh after `check_diff_size()`: Phase S gate between quality checks and commit
  - SPIRAL_SECURITY_SCAN=false → immediate return 0 (no-op)
  - Scanner binary not found → skip with warning, return 0 (not a failure)
  - No staged files → skip, return 0
  - Runs `semgrep --config=auto --json --output=<path> <staged_files>` or `bandit -r <py_files> -f json -o <path>`
  - HIGH findings (semgrep: ERROR severity; bandit: HIGH issue_severity) → return 1 (fail)
  - MEDIUM findings (semgrep: WARNING; bandit: MEDIUM) → emit warning, return 0
  - Results written to `.spiral/security_scan_{STORY_ID}.json`
- Inserted `run_security_scan` gate in main loop after `check_diff_size` and before `do_git_commit`, with same unstage/retry/prd.json pattern as other gates
- Created `tests/security_scan.bats` with 10 tests: all pass

### Patterns discovered
- `run_security_scan` uses `git diff --cached --name-only` (staged files, BEFORE commit) not `git diff --name-only HEAD~1`
- semgrep HIGH severity maps to `.extra.severity == "ERROR"` in JSON output; bandit HIGH maps to `.issue_severity == "HIGH"`
- SPIRAL_SCRATCH_DIR already created by the time the gate runs (created by run_secret_scan earlier)
- bats stub for `command -v <tool>`: override `command()` function to return 0/1 based on args

### Gotchas
- semgrep maps HIGH→"ERROR", MEDIUM→"WARNING" (not "HIGH"/"MEDIUM") in its JSON output `.extra.severity`
- bandit only processes Python files; non-Python staged files are silently skipped
- `$staged_files` is unquoted in the scanner call (intentional: passes as separate args)
- test_route_stories.py has pre-existing import error (not related to this story) — run pytest with --ignore

## Iteration N - Story: US-106: Add story dependency auto-inference from filesTouch overlap

### What was implemented
- Created `lib/infer_dependencies.py`: Jaccard similarity scan of pending story filesTouch pairs
  - Strong (>= 0.5): written to prd.json deps when SPIRAL_AUTO_INFER_DEPS=true
  - Weak (> 0 but < 0.5): written to --out-hints JSON file
  - Uses `find_cycles()` from check_dag.py before writing any edge (cycle prevention)
- Wired call in spiral.sh Phase M after post-merge assertions (line ~1484)
- Added `SPIRAL_AUTO_INFER_DEPS="${SPIRAL_AUTO_INFER_DEPS:-false}"` env var default
- 26 unit tests in tests/test_infer_dependencies.py — all pass; full suite 501 passed

### Patterns discovered
- Jaccard: use `len(a & b) / len(a | b)` — same threshold as technical notes (0.5 strong, >0 weak)
- apply_strong_deps early-exits if either direction already recorded (`b_id in deps_a or a_id in deps_b`)
- `find_cycles()` checks the ENTIRE graph — so a pre-existing cycle blocks ALL new edge applications
- Phase M call uses `|| true` guard so a non-zero exit doesn't abort the spiral

### Gotchas
- "Both directions create a cycle" only happens when the base graph already contains a cycle
  (find_cycles is global, not per-edge). The test must set up a pre-existing cycle.
- spiral.sh Phase M structure: the infer_dependencies call goes INSIDE the `else` block
  (after `write_checkpoint`) but BEFORE the closing `fi` of "end validation else"

- Added help text entry for `--log-level`

### Patterns discovered

- The `level_field` local in `log_spiral_event()` is placed before trace_fields so it appears near the top of each JSON entry

## Iteration N - Story: US-132: Add SPIRAL_PRE_PHASE_HOOK and SPIRAL_POST_PHASE_HOOK for user-defined phase scripts

### What was implemented
- Added `SPIRAL_PRE_PHASE_HOOK`, `SPIRAL_POST_PHASE_HOOK`, `SPIRAL_HOOK_TIMEOUT` env vars to spiral.sh defaults section
- Added `run_phase_hook PRE|POST PHASE` function after `notify_webhook` in spiral.sh
  - Checks if hook is set and executable (skips with warning if not)
  - Exports SPIRAL_CURRENT_PHASE, SPIRAL_CURRENT_STORY_ID, SPIRAL_RUN_ID, SPIRAL_ITERATION to hook
  - Runs hook with `timeout ${SPIRAL_HOOK_TIMEOUT:-30}`
  - Logs `phase_hook_pre` / `phase_hook_post` events with exit_code and duration_s to spiral_events.jsonl
  - PRE hook non-zero exit emits error message; POST hook non-zero exit emits warning
- Added `run_phase_hook PRE "X" || continue` calls at phases R, M, G, I, V (pre-hook failure aborts iteration)
- Added `run_phase_hook POST "X" || true` calls at phases R, M, G/I, V (post-hook failure is non-fatal)
- Documented in `templates/spiral.config.example.sh` with hook contract, env vars, and example scripts
- Added 5 bats tests in `tests/spiral_phases.bats` covering: post-hook called, pre-hook 0 allows continue, SPIRAL_CURRENT_PHASE logged, non-executable hook skipped, SPIRAL_HOOK_TIMEOUT respected

### Patterns discovered
- `run_phase_hook PRE "X" || continue` pattern is clean for aborting story attempt on pre-hook failure
- `_NEXT_SID` is only set inside Phase I (empty for earlier phases); exporting `${_NEXT_SID:-}` is safe
- Post-hooks for G and I are both called since they share a combined G/I block in spiral.sh
- `|| true` is sufficient to make post-hooks non-fatal

### Gotchas
- Phase G and Phase I share `_PHASE_TS_I` timestamp and `phase_end` events; POST hooks for both fire before their respective `phase_end` events
- The pre-hook for Phase I fires inside a deeply nested block (4 levels) but `continue` still correctly reaches the outer while loop


## Iteration N - Story: US-152: Validate prd.json for non-UTF-8 bytes and control characters at startup

### What was implemented
- Created `lib/check_prd_encoding.py` with `check_encoding(path)` and `sanitize_prd(path)` functions
- `check_encoding()` validates UTF-8 validity, JSON parsability, and scans all string values for control chars (0x00-0x08, 0x0B-0x0C, 0x0E-0x1F); allows tab (0x09), newline (0x0A)
- Returns list of `{path, char, pos}` dicts for each offending character
- `sanitize_prd()` strips control characters in-place and rewrites file; returns True if changed
- CLI supports `--sanitize` flag and `--quiet` flag; exit codes: 0=clean, 1=IO/parse error, 2=issues found
- Added encoding check block to `validate_preflight.sh` after schema check; reads `SPIRAL_SANITIZE_PRD` env var to pass `--sanitize` flag; aborts on enc_rc != 0
- Written 16 tests in `tests/test_prd_encoding.py` covering: clean files pass, unicode allowed, tab/newline allowed, null byte detected, various control chars, path in issue dict, non-UTF-8 raises, missing file raises, invalid JSON raises, sanitize strips, no-change on clean, valid unicode preserved, rewritten JSON parseable, post-sanitize check_encoding passes

### Patterns discovered
- `_CTRL_RE = re.compile(r"[\x00-\x08\x0b\x0c\x0e-\x1f]")` is the correct control-char pattern excluding tab/newline/CR
- `${sanitize_flag}` (no quotes) in bash safely expands to empty string when unset — correct for optional flags
- Redirect both stdout and stderr of encoding check into enc_out via `2>&1` then echo on non-empty; this unifies error messages through the preflight echo format

### Gotchas
- json.dump with control chars in string values: Python's json module *does* escape control chars as \uXXXX sequences when writing — so the JSON file itself won't contain raw bytes, but the parsed Python string *will* contain the actual character. check_encoding reads back parsed data so it catches them correctly.
- Test assertion: "Café\x00café" minus \x00 = "Cafécafé" not "Caféé" (initial test was wrong — caught before commit)
- Full suite: 554 passed, 2 skipped — no regressions

## Iteration N - Story: US-142: Add `spiral.sh --rollback STORY_ID` to revert a passed story's commit

### What was implemented
- Added `ERR_ROLLBACK_FAILED=12` error code constant to spiral.sh
- Added `ROLLBACK_STORY_ID=""` default variable to argument parsing section
- Added `--rollback STORY_ID` argument parsing case (alongside `--replay`)
- Added `--rollback STORY_ID` to `--help` output
- Added rollback implementation block in spiral.sh (after --replay block, before startup):
  - Validates story exists in prd.json (exits ERR_STORY_NOT_FOUND=11 if not)
  - Guards against dirty working tree using `git status --porcelain | grep -v '^??'` (tracked files only, excludes untracked)
  - Reads `_passedCommit` SHA; exits ERR_ROLLBACK_FAILED=12 with actionable message if absent
  - Runs `git revert --no-edit <sha>` to create a revert commit (preserves linear history)
  - Clears `passes`, `_passedCommit`, `_passedAt`, `_adrPath` from story using jq `|=` with `del()`
  - Logs `rollback_complete` event to spiral_events.jsonl
- Added 4 bats tests in `tests/test_rollback.bats` covering:
  - Successful rollback: git revert created, prd.json passes=false, _passedCommit absent
  - Missing _passedCommit: exits 12 with "no _passedCommit" message
  - Dirty working-tree guard (modified tracked file): exits 12 with "uncommitted changes" message
  - Story not found: exits 11 with "not found" message

### Patterns discovered
- Untracked files (`??` in git status) should NOT trigger the dirty tree guard — filter with `grep -v '^??'`
- On Windows MSYS2/Git Bash, `/tmp/...` paths from `mktemp` are MSYS2 paths that native Python cannot resolve; use `os.path.join(os.getcwd(), 'filename')` in bats test Python assertions instead
- bats test assertions that run Python scripts must avoid MSYS2 path strings — use relative paths (os.getcwd()) since each test `cd "$TEST_REPO"` first
- jq `|= (.passes = false | del(._passedCommit) | del(._passedAt) | del(._adrPath))` works correctly for multi-field update + deletion
- ERR_ROLLBACK_FAILED=12 added to error code table in spiral.sh header comment

### Gotchas
- The dirty tree guard must use `grep -v '^??'` to exclude untracked files; otherwise test repos (with prd.json and spiral.config.sh as untracked files) would always fail the guard
- `echo "$_RB_UPDATED" > "$PRD_FILE"` correctly writes jq output to prd.json even with `exec > >(tee ...)` active (explicit `>` redirect overrides the exec redirect for that command)
- The rollback block must come AFTER `log_spiral_event` is defined (sourced from lib/spiral_events.sh at line 891) and AFTER `exec > >(tee ...)` at line 662
- Pre-existing test flakiness: test_partition.py and test_check_dag.py have Hypothesis health check failures (slow input generation) that are unrelated to this story


## Iteration N - Story: US-153: Add `spiral status` subcommand with color-coded story progress table

### What was implemented
- Rewrote `cmd_status` in `main.py` to produce a full color-coded story progress table
- Added `--json` flag to the `status` subparser for machine-readable output
- `_classify_stories()` bucketes stories into passed / in_progress / skipped / pending:
  - passed: `passes == true`
  - skipped: `_skipped == true`
  - in_progress: `passes == false` AND `retry_counts[id] > 0`
  - pending: `passes == false` AND no retries
- `_avg_retries()` computes average retry count per status group from `retry-counts.json`
- `_render_rich()` uses the `rich` library when available (already installed as transitive dep)
- `_render_plain()` stdlib-only fallback with aligned columns
- Both renderers respect `NO_COLOR` env var (rich does so natively; plain skips ANSI)
- Header shows `SPIRAL_RUN_ID` (from checkpoint or env var) and current iteration (from checkpoint → results.tsv fallback)
- Loads only prd.json, results.tsv, retry-counts.json, and .spiral/_checkpoint.json — no API calls
- 18 tests in `tests/test_main.py` covering: all status rows present, correct counts, run_id in header, iteration from results.tsv, --json structure, per-bucket counts, avg_retry_count, percentage sums, classification logic, missing prd.json, performance < 1s

### Patterns discovered
- `rich` is already a transitive dependency (installed in .venv) even though it's not in pyproject.toml directly — safe to import with `try: import rich`
- `SimpleNamespace(json=False)` is the cleanest way to mock args objects in pytest for argparse-based CLIs
- Patching `main.PRD_FILE`, `main.RETRY_COUNTS`, `main.RESULTS_TSV`, `main.CHECKPOINT_FILE` as module-level Path objects is clean and testable

### Gotchas
- `rich.__version__` AttributeError on some installations — use `import rich` without version check
- `_USE_COLOUR` is module-level global set at import time; tests that patch `os.environ["NO_COLOR"]` after import won't affect it — tests should use `_args()` helper and patch module paths instead
- 1 pre-existing Hypothesis flake in `test_partition.py` (slow input gen) — unrelated to this story; 568 passed otherwise

- `_NEXT_SID` is already set earlier in Phase I (sequential and parallel wave single-story paths)
- `jq -Rsc 'split("\n") | map(select(. != ""))'` is the cleanest way to convert a newline-separated shell list to a JSON array

- Added `create_github_pr()` function to ralph/ralph.sh (after `append_result` function)
- Function guards: gh CLI not in PATH → SKIP with actionable message; gh not authenticated → SKIP with actionable message
- Pushes story commit to `spiral/<STORY_ID>` branch via `git push origin <sha>:refs/heads/<branch> --force`
- Auto-creates `spiral-ai` label if missing (best-effort, non-fatal)
- Checks for existing PR via `gh pr list --head <branch>` to be idempotent on retries
- Creates PR with: title from story title, body includes description + acceptance criteria + SPIRAL_RUN_ID + commit SHA
- Stores PR URL in prd.json as `_prUrl` field using jq

- Rollback (spiral.sh --rollback): also clears `_prUrl` from prd.json alongside other fields

### Patterns discovered
- `eval "$(sed -n '/^function_name()/,/^}/p' script.sh)"` is the reliable way to source a single function from a .sh file in bats tests
- Use `"$FAKE_BIN_DIR:$PATH"` in `env PATH=...` to inject mock binaries
- gh pr list with `--json url --jq '.[0].url'` returns empty when no PR exists; filter output with `grep -E '^https?://'` for robustness
- prd.json schema validation runs during preflight (before rollback executes); test prd.json must include all required fields (acceptanceCriteria, dependencies)

### Gotchas
- `case "$1 $2"` in bats stubs works well for gh subcommands; make pr list return empty string (not `[]`) for "no existing PR" case
- `git push origin <sha>:refs/heads/<branch> --force` is idempotent (retries won't fail if branch already exists at same SHA)
- The create_github_pr function must come BEFORE it is first called in the file; placed after append_result() (line ~794)



## Iteration N - Story: US-123: Stream-process large prd.json with jq --stream to avoid full in-memory parse

### What was implemented
- Added `SPIRAL_PRD_STREAM_THRESHOLD_KB` (default 512) config default to ralph/ralph.sh
- Added `get_pending_story_ids()` function in ralph.sh:
  - Checks prd.json file size in KB via `wc -c`
  - When file_kb >= threshold_kb (and threshold > 0): uses `jq -rn --stream` with `fromstream(1|truncate_stream(...))` to reconstruct story objects without full parse, filters, sorts via shell `sort`, cuts ID column
  - When below threshold: uses normal full-in-memory jq parse
  - Both paths call `tr -d '\r'` to strip Windows carriage returns
- Replaced direct jq call at `ALL_INCOMPLETE=` with `get_pending_story_ids "$PRD_FILE"`
- Documented `SPIRAL_PRD_STREAM_THRESHOLD_KB` in spiral.config.sh (commented section)
- Updated `lib/spiral_doctor.sh` to check jq version >= 1.6 (required for --stream)
- Added `tests/prd_stream.bats` with 9 tests: priority sort (both paths), excludes passed/decomposed, empty set, and equivalence test on 50-story synthetic PRD

### Patterns discovered
- `jq -rn --stream` + `fromstream(1|truncate_stream(inputs|select(.[0][0]=="userStories")))` is the canonical idiom for streaming array elements from a large JSON file
- Both normal and streaming paths produce identical sorted output because jq's `sort_by(.priority)` and shell `sort` both sort alphabetically (critical < high < low < medium)
- `wc -c` gives byte count; dividing by 1024 gives KB — portable and fast

### Gotchas
- On Windows/MSYS2, jq outputs \r\n line endings — must call `tr -d '\r'` inside `get_pending_story_ids` (not just at the call site) so bats tests pass without extra stripping
- `SPIRAL_PRD_STREAM_THRESHOLD_KB=0` forces the streaming path (useful for testing)
- `test_route_stories.py` has a pre-existing relative import failure (excluded from test run); 569 passed otherwise

## Iteration N - Story: US-144: Add Ollama local LLM fallback when Claude API is unreachable

### What was implemented
- Added `SPIRAL_OLLAMA_FALLBACK_MODEL` (default: empty/disabled) and `SPIRAL_OLLAMA_HOST` (default: `http://localhost:11434/v1`) config defaults to ralph.sh
- Added `call_ollama_fallback(sys_file, usr_file)` function in ralph.sh — builds JSON payload via python3, POSTs to Ollama OpenAI-compat endpoint, extracts response content
- Added `_CLAUDE_API_FAIL_STREAK=0` counter before main loop; resets to 0 on each story start
- Added connection failure detection inside `_529_ATTEMPT` loop: empty `_CLAUDE_TMP` or ECONNREFUSED/ETIMEDOUT patterns → increment streak; at streak >= 3, call `call_ollama_fallback` and set `_OLLAMA_USED=1`
- Added `_model: ollama/<model>` tagging in prd.json after story passes when `_OLLAMA_USED=1`
- Added Ollama reachability check to `lib/spiral_doctor.sh` using `curl` against `<host>/api/tags`; emits [WARN] when SPIRAL_OLLAMA_FALLBACK_MODEL configured but Ollama unreachable
- Written 8 bats tests in `tests/test_ollama_fallback.bats` covering: default vars, curl exit 7/28 detection, successful response extraction, custom host logging, doctor warn/ok

### Patterns discovered
- `call_ollama_fallback` uses temp files for system/user prompts (not env vars) to avoid arg-list-too-long for large prompts
- `response=$(curl -sf ... 2>/dev/null)` captures body; `curl_rc=$?` captures exit code — cleaner than 2>&1
- Bats tests cannot inspect `response=$(...)` capture — check the function's direct `echo` output instead
- connection failure check fires BEFORE 529 detection (ordering matters; empty file ≠ overloaded)

### Gotchas
- Connection failure check only runs when `SPIRAL_OLLAMA_FALLBACK_MODEL` is non-empty (guard); no performance cost when disabled
- `_OLLAMA_USED=0` reset must happen per-story (added right after `STORY_START=$(date +%s)`)
- `${ollama_base%/v1}` strips `/v1` suffix to get base URL for Ollama's native `/api/tags` endpoint
- 569 pytest passed, 8 new bats tests all pass

## Pre-analysis for US-173 (Gemini 2.5 Pro)
This brief outlines the implementation plan for story US-173 in the Spiral project. The context is a Shell and Python-based workflow, not a Frappe application.

**1. Files to Modify:**
*   `spiral.sh`: To integrate the new validation phase into the main pipeline.
*   `lib/phases/phase_s_story_validate.sh`: Implement the logic for the validation phase, orchestrating the validation process.
*   `lib/merge_stories.py` (or similar for Phase M): Update to consume the validated stories file instead of the raw research output.
*   New Python script (e.g., `lib/story_validator.py`): To house the core validation logic, including the LLM call and keyword fallback.
*   New BATS test (e.g., `tests/story_validation.bats`): To verify the feature's acceptance criteria.

**2. Involved DocTypes/Hooks:**
*   This is not a Frappe project. The primary data structures are JSON files:
    *   `prd.json`: Source for project `goals`.
    *   Input stories from the research phase.
    *   `.spiral/_validated_stories.json`: The output artifact of this new phase.

**3. Implementation Approach:**
1.  In `spiral.sh`, insert a call to `run_phase_story_validate()` between Phase T (Research) and Phase M (Merge).
2.  The `phase_s_story_validate.sh` script will invoke a new Python script.
3.  The Python script will iterate through each candidate story, checking it against `prd.json` goals (and the constitution if `SPIRAL_SPECKIT_CONSTITUTION` is set) using a Claude Haiku API call with a direct YES/NO prompt.
4.  If the API call fails, the script must fall back to a simple keyword overlap check.
5.  Accepted stories are written to `.spiral/_validated_stories.json`. Phase M's input source must be updated to this file.
6.  Rejected stories and the reason must be logged, and metrics written to `spiral_events.jsonl`.

**4. Edge Cases & Gotchas:**
*   The LLM prompt must be carefully engineered to force a reliable YES/NO output.
*   The keyword fallback logic needs to be robust enough to handle API failures without causing false positives/negatives.
*   Ensure logging is clear, providing auditable reasons for every story rejection.
*   The new phase adds latency; performance should be considered, especially the external API call for each story.

1.  In `spiral.sh`, add a call to `run_phase_story_validate()` after Phase T completes.

## Pre-analysis for US-182 (Gemini 2.5 Pro)
Based on my analysis of the user story and the project structure, here is a technical brief for the implementing agent.

**Project:** Spiral (Workflow Orchestrator)
**User Story:** US-182: Parallelize Phase R and Phase T

### 1. Core Implementation Files
*   **`spiral.sh`**: This is the main orchestration script where the sequential calls to Phase R and Phase T likely reside. The core logic for backgrounding jobs, capturing PIDs, and waiting will be implemented here.
*   **`lib/state_machine.py` / `prd.json`**: The state machine handles phase transitions and checkpointing. It will need to be modified to recognize and record the new, separate completion flags (`phase_r_done`, `phase_t_done`) in the `prd.json` state file.
*   **`tests/spiral_phases.bats`**: A new or existing BATS test file should be used to create a test case with mock Phase R and Phase T scripts to verify parallel execution and correct failure handling.

### 2. Involved Components
*   **Shell Functions (in `spiral.sh`):** `run_phase_r` and `run_phase_t` (or similarly named functions/script calls).
*   **State Management:** The `prd.json` file serves as the checkpointing database. The schema and the Python code that writes to it will need updating.

### 3. Recommended Implementation Approach
1.  In `spiral.sh`, locate the sequential execution block for phases R and T.
2.  Modify the block to launch each phase as a background process using `&`, capturing their respective `PID`s. Example: `run_phase_r > "$LOG_DIR/phase_r.log" 2>&1 & PID_R=$!`.
3.  Use `wait $PID_R` and `wait $PID_T` to await the completion of both processes before proceeding to Phase M. Capture the exit code (`$?`) immediately after each `wait`.
4.  Update `lib/state_machine.py` to check for and write `phase_r_done` and `phase_t_done` Booleans to `prd.json`, allowing the system to correctly resume if interrupted.
5.  In the logging/banner logic, calculate the wall time using the start time before parallel execution and the end time after the final `wait`.

### 4. Edge Cases & Gotchas
*   **Failure Handling:** The script must not exit if one of the parallel phases fails. It should capture the non-zero exit code, mark that specific phase as incomplete in the state file, and allow the workflow to proceed to the reporting/failure-handling stage.
*   **Resource Contention:** Running both phases at once may strain CPU or memory. This could lead to swapping or context-switching overhead, potentially negating the time savings on resource-constrained systems.
*   **Log Management:** Ensure both `stdout` and `stderr` for each phase are redirected to separate log files (e.g., `phase_r.log`, `phase_t.log`) to prevent interleaved and unreadable output.
*   **Atomic State:** The checkpointing update should be as atomic as possible to prevent a race condition where the script is terminated after one phase finishes but before the state file is updated.


## Iteration 50 - Story: US-182: Run Phase R and Phase T in parallel to halve story-preparation wall time

### What was implemented
- `spiral.sh` — Replaced sequential Phase R + Phase T blocks with parallel execution:
  - Both phases are launched as background jobs (`& PID_R=$!`, `& PID_T=$!`) after skip checks
  - All output is buffered to `_phase_r_bg.log` / `_phase_t_bg.log` and printed in order after both complete
  - Each job writes an independent checkpoint marker file (`_phase_R_N.ckpt`, `_phase_T_N.ckpt`)
  - Each job records end timestamp to `_phase_R_N.endtime` / `_phase_T_N.endtime` for accurate individual durations
  - `wait $PID_R; RC_R=$?` + `wait $PID_T; RC_T=$?` collect exit codes; failures produce empty output (not fatal)
  - `write_checkpoint "$SPIRAL_ITER" "T"` written once after both jobs complete
  - `_PHASE_DUR_RT_WALL` = actual wall time (≈ max(R,T)); banner shows `[R+T wall=Ns]`
  - PRE hook for Phase R remains synchronous (|| continue still aborts iteration if hook fails)
  - POST hook for Phase R runs after both phases complete
- `checkpoint_phase_done()` — Updated to check `_phase_R_N.ckpt` / `_phase_T_N.ckpt` marker files before falling back to main checkpoint, enabling independent resume
- `tests/phase_parallel_rt.bats` — New bats test: mock Claude (2s sleep) + mock synthesize (1s sleep), verifies T starts before R finishes (|t_start - r_start| < 2s)

### Patterns discovered
- Background job subshells inherit ALL parent shell variables and functions at fork time — no need to re-export
- Use separate temp log files per background job to prevent output interleaving; cat them in order after wait
- Record end timestamps to files so parent can compute individual durations after both jobs complete
- `write_checkpoint` must be called from parent (not subshell) to avoid race condition on checkpoint file

### Gotchas
- `|| continue` in PRE hook MUST remain in parent shell (not inside subshell) — subshell continue aborts only the subshell, not the outer while loop
- `wait $PID_R; RC_R=$?` must use braces: `{ wait "$PID_R"; RC_R=$?; }` to capture correct exit code
- `_patch_parallel_rt.py` is a one-off helper script — added to .gitignore or delete after use

## Pre-analysis for US-136 (Gemini 2.5 Pro)
### Technical Brief: US-136 Workspace Cleanup

This story is a shell-script-based task, not a Frappe/Python one. All modifications will be within the existing `spiral` shell scripting framework.

**1. Files to Modify:**
*   `spiral.sh`: This is the main entry point. The new `cleanup_workspace()` function and its invocation will be added here.
*   `spiral_events.sh` (optional): May be used to abstract the event logging, but direct logging from `spiral.sh` is also acceptable per technical notes.

**2. Frappe DocTypes / Hooks:**
*   None. This task does not involve the Frappe framework.

**3. Recommended Implementation Approach:**
1.  In `spiral.sh`, create a new bash function `cleanup_workspace()`.
2.  At the end of the main execution loop, after run completion is determined, add a condition to call this function if `[[ "$SPIRAL_WORKSPACE_CLEANUP" == "true" ]]`.
3.  Inside `cleanup_workspace()`:
    *   First, confirm 100% of stories in `results.tsv` are `passed` or `skipped`.
    *   Get pre-cleanup size: `before_size=$(du -sb .spiral/ | cut -f1)`.
    *   Use `find .spiral/research_cache -mtime +${SPIRAL_CACHE_TTL:-7} -delete` for cache pruning.
    *   Use `find .spiral -name "*.log" -size 0 -delete` for empty logs.
    *   Ensure `.spiral/archive` exists (`mkdir -p`), then archive old summaries via `tar`.
    *   Get post-cleanup size: `after_size=$(du -sb .spiral/ | cut -f1)`.
    *   Calculate `bytes_freed=$((before_size - after_size))`.
    *   Log the event: `echo '{"event":"workspace_cleanup", "bytes_freed":'${bytes_freed}'}' >> .spiral/spiral_events.jsonl`.

**4. Edge Cases & Gotchas:**
*   The completion check must be robust; ensure it correctly parses `results.tsv` and doesn't trigger on in-progress runs.
*   The `tar` command will fail if the `.spiral/archive/` directory doesn't exist. Use `mkdir -p`.
*   The `find` commands must be carefully scoped to the `.spiral/` directory to avoid accidentally deleting files from other parts of the workspace.
*   Ensure the script gracefully handles cases where there are no files to delete or archive.
